This book has been heavily criticized on theoretical and methodological grounds, but some of its findings<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> have been confirmed by further empirical research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jost_et_al._2003_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jost_et_al._2003-196">[196]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1973, British psychologist <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Wilson_(psychologist)" title="Glenn Wilson (psychologist)">Glenn Wilson</a> published an influential book providing evidence that a general factor underlying conservative beliefs is "fear of uncertainty."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> A meta-analysis of research literature by Jost, Glaser, Kruglanski, and Sulloway in 2003 found that many factors, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ambiguity_tolerance" title="Ambiguity tolerance">intolerance of ambiguity</a> and need for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cognitive_closure_(psychology)" title="Cognitive closure (psychology)">cognitive closure</a>, contribute to the degree of one's political conservatism and its manifestations in decision-making.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jost_et_al._2003_196-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jost_et_al._2003-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> A study by Kathleen Maclay stated these traits "might be associated with such generally valued characteristics as personal commitment and unwavering loyalty". The research also suggested that while most people are resistant to change, liberals are more tolerant of it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to psychologist <a href="/wiki/Bob_Altemeyer" title="Bob Altemeyer">Bob Altemeyer</a>, individuals who are politically conservative tend to rank high in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-wing_authoritarianism" title="Right-wing authoritarianism">right-wing authoritarianism</a> (RWA) on his RWA scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> This finding was echoed by Adorno. A study done on Israeli and Palestinian students in Israel found that RWA scores of right-wing party supporters were significantly higher than those of left-wing party supporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> However, a 2005 study by H. Michael Crowson and colleagues suggested a moderate gap between RWA and other conservative positions, stating that their "results indicated that conservatism is not synonymous with RWA".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>
</p><p>Psychologist Felicia Pratto and her colleagues have found evidence to support the idea that a high <a href="/wiki/Social_dominance_orientation" title="Social dominance orientation">social dominance orientation</a> (SDO) is strongly correlated with conservative political views and opposition to social engineering to promote equality,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pratto_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-pratto-203">[203]</a></sup> though Pratto's findings have been highly controversial<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> as Pratto and her colleagues found that high SDO scores were highly correlated with measures of <a href="/wiki/Prejudice" title="Prejudice">prejudice</a>. However, <a href="/wiki/David_J._Schneider" title="David J. Schneider">David J. Schneider</a> argued for a more complex relationships between the three factors, writing that "correlations between prejudice and political conservative are reduced virtually to zero when controls for SDO are instituted, suggesting that the conservatism–prejudice link is caused by SDO".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> Conservative political theorist <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Minogue" title="Kenneth Minogue">Kenneth Minogue</a> criticized Pratto's work, saying: "It is characteristic of the conservative temperament to value established identities, to praise habit and to respect prejudice, not because it is irrational, but because such things anchor the darting impulses of human beings in solidities of custom which we do not often begin to value until we are already losing them. Radicalism often generates youth movements, while conservatism is a condition found among the mature, who have discovered what it is in life they most value".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup>
</p><p>A 1996 study on the relationship between racism and conservatism found that the correlation was stronger among more educated individuals, though "anti-Black affect had essentially no relationship with political conservatism at any level of educational or intellectual sophistication". They also found that the correlation between racism and conservatism could be entirely accounted for by their mutual relationship with social dominance orientation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sidanius96_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-sidanius96-206">[206]</a></sup>
</p><p>In his 2008 book, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_C._Brooks#Gross_National_Happiness" title="Arthur C. Brooks"><i>Gross National Happiness</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_C._Brooks" title="Arthur C. Brooks">Arthur C. Brooks</a> presents the finding that conservatives are roughly twice as happy as liberals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> A 2008 study demonstrates that conservatives tend to be happier than liberals because of their tendency to justify the current state of affairs and because they're less bothered by inequalities in society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-napier_and_jost_2008_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-napier_and_jost_2008-208">[208]</a></sup> In fact, as income inequality increases, this difference in relative happiness increases because conservatives, more so than liberals, possess an ideological buffer against the negative hedonic effects of <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">economic inequality</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-napier_and_jost_2008_208-1"><a href="#cite_note-napier_and_jost_2008-208">[208]</a></sup> A 2012 study disputed this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2009 study found that conservatism and cognitive ability are negatively correlated. It found that conservatism has a negative correlation with <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a>, Vocabulary, and Analogy test scores, measures of education (such as gross enrollment in <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">primary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education" title="Tertiary education">tertiary</a> levels), and performance on math and reading assignments from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PISA" title="PISA">PISA</a>. It also found that conservatism correlates with components of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Failed_States_Index" title="Failed States Index">Failed States Index</a> and "several other measures of economic and political development of nations."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stankov2009_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stankov2009-210">[210]</a></sup> This study used participants from 74 countries and a different definition of conservatism than other similar studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stankov2009_210-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stankov2009-210">[210]</a></sup> The definition of which loadings constitute conservativism vary throughout the study.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stankov2009_210-2"><a href="#cite_note-Stankov2009-210">[210]</a></sup>  Nonetheless, in a Brazilian sample, the highest IQs were found among <a href="/wiki/Centre-right_politics" title="Centre-right politics">centre-rightists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Centrism" title="Centrism">centrists</a>, even after correcting for gender, age, education and income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup>
</p><p>Personality psychology research has shown that conservatism is positively correlated to <a href="/wiki/Conscientiousness" title="Conscientiousness">conscientiousness</a> and negatively correlated with <a href="/wiki/Openness_to_experience" title="Openness to experience">openness to new experiences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-politics_meta-analysis_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-politics_meta-analysis-214">[214]</a></sup> Because conscientiousness is positively related to job performance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> a 2021 study found that conservative service workers earn higher ratings, evaluations, and tips than liberal ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">McLean, Iain; McMillan, Alistair (2009). It can take a 'reactionary' form, harking back to, and attempting to reconstruct, forms of society which existed in an earlier period". <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-920516-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-920516-5">978-0-19-920516-5</a>.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-72">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">ams, Ian Political Ideology Today (2nd edition), Manchester University Press, 2002, p. 46</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-73"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-73">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFawcett2020">Fawcett, Edmund (October 20, 2020). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TO3eDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Conservatism: The Fight for a Tradition</i></a>. Princeton University Press. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5"><bdi>978-0-691-17410-5</bdi></a>. <q>Little of that, though fascinating, would have won Chateaubriand a place in the story of conservatism had he not he passed down to it a repertoire of disavowal for the “empty world” of liberal modernity and a counterpart trust in the “full heart” of faith and loyalty. Chateaubriand was a Romantic among conservatism’s anti-rationalist forerunners.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Conservatism%3A+The+Fight+for+a+Tradition&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2020-10-20&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-691-17410-5&amp;rft.aulast=Fawcett&amp;rft.aufirst=Edmund&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DTO3eDwAAQBAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AConservatism"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-74">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFawcett2020">Fawcett, Edmund (October 20, 2020). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TO3eDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Conservatism: The Fight for a Tradition</i></a>. Princeton University Press. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5"><bdi>978-0-691-17410-5</bdi></a>. <q>Gentz did not mock the Declaration of the Rights of Man in the satirical manner of Justus Möser (1720–94), the north-Saxon critic of market society and Enlightenment princely reform. Nor did Gentz fault the declaration, as Burke had done, for misunderstanding the character of rights. Gentz instead subjected the declaration to an article-by-article critique (1793) for errors of drafting and logic</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Conservatism%3A+The+Fight+for+a+Tradition&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2020-10-20&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-691-17410-5&amp;rft.aulast=Fawcett&amp;rft.aufirst=Edmund&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DTO3eDwAAQBAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AConservatism"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFawcett2020">Fawcett, Edmund (October 20, 2020). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TO3eDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Conservatism: The Fight for a Tradition</i></a>. Princeton University Press. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5"><bdi>978-0-691-17410-5</bdi></a>. <q>Less well-known thinkers who influenced later German conservatives were against revolution from the outset. August Rehberg (1757–1836) was a German Burkean and scholar from Hanover who took the Revolution to be antihistorical . . . Müller’s hopes for preserving Germany’s legally privileged classes, its old “estates,” and restoring an imagined premodern unity struck Gentz as out of touch . . . The Revolution took a wrong turn, left history’s “rational” march for freedom, and slipped into violent unreason. The Terror, on that understanding, was a contingent horror, as a little part of intelligible human history, Hegel wrote, as “chopping the head off a cabbage.” . . . After his death, Hegel’s heritage divided like the French assembly into right and left.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Conservatism%3A+The+Fight+for+a+Tradition&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2020-10-20&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-691-17410-5&amp;rft.aulast=Fawcett&amp;rft.aufirst=Edmund&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DTO3eDwAAQBAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AConservatism"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-76">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFawcett2020">Fawcett, Edmund (October 20, 2020). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TO3eDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Conservatism: The Fight for a Tradition</i></a>. Princeton University Press. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5"><bdi>978-0-691-17410-5</bdi></a>. <q>Neither Burke nor Maistre believed that people in general were capable of self-government, though for different reasons.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Conservatism%3A+The+Fight+for+a+Tradition&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2020-10-20&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-691-17410-5&amp;rft.aulast=Fawcett&amp;rft.aufirst=Edmund&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DTO3eDwAAQBAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AConservatism"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-77">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFawcett2020">Fawcett, Edmund (October 20, 2020). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TO3eDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Conservatism: The Fight for a Tradition</i></a>. Princeton University Press. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5"><bdi>978-0-691-17410-5</bdi></a>. <q>Maistre took a bleak view of unregenerate humanity. It could never be relied on to keep the rules and it needed harsh discipline and submissive faith together with the threat of swift punishment. . . .The trouble with trusting people to govern themselves lay for Burke not in their inability to keep rules but in their incapacity to make rules.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Conservatism%3A+The+Fight+for+a+Tradition&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2020-10-20&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-691-17410-5&amp;rft.aulast=Fawcett&amp;rft.aufirst=Edmund&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DTO3eDwAAQBAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AConservatism"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-78">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFawcett2020">Fawcett, Edmund (October 20, 2020). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TO3eDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Conservatism: The Fight for a Tradition</i></a>. Princeton University Press. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5"><bdi>978-0-691-17410-5</bdi></a>. <q>Whether the rules of society came from a divine source, as Maistre insisted, or from custom, as Burke held</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Conservatism%3A+The+Fight+for+a+Tradition&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2020-10-20&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-691-17410-5&amp;rft.aulast=Fawcett&amp;rft.aufirst=Edmund&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DTO3eDwAAQBAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AConservatism"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFawcett2020">Fawcett, Edmund (October 20, 2020). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TO3eDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Conservatism: The Fight for a Tradition</i></a>. Princeton University Press. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-691-17410-5"><bdi>978-0-691-17410-5</bdi></a>. <q>It was plain to Burke that, once freed from custom and good sense, people were capable of the worst follies and crimes. Maistre thought the same once people were freed from God and his earthly ministers..</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Conservatism%3A+The+Fight+for+a+Tradition&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2020-10-20&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-691-17410-5&amp;rft.aulast=Fawcett&amp;rft.aufirst=Edmund&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DTO3eDwAAQBAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AConservatism"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-80">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFawcett2020">Fawcett, Edmund (October 20, 2020). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TO3eDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Conservatism: The Fight for a Tradition</i></a>. <li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFawcett2020">Fawcett, Edmund (October 20, 2020). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TO3eDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Conservatism: The Fight for a Tradition</i></a>. <li id="cite_note-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-82">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFawcett2020">Fawcett, Edmund (October 20, 2020). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=TO3eDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Conservatism: The Fight for a Tradition</i></a>.
